Very traditional ‚Äúomakase‚Äù sushi bar experience right here in the Rancho district. Staff speaks minimal English, the prices are high, the decor rustic and a bit dusty. But it is VERY GOOD! Chef will serve you a nice variety of small plates, advise you what sauce to use for each and what each is called. Fair warning: if you‚Äôre not careful, you could easily drop $150 per person in a hour of steady eating and drinking. You can always choose to sit at a booth and order a la carte to keep total costs down a bit.< /review>

< Review>
The experience and tasty fresh sushi deserves 5 stars, not to mention the attention and service we received. The high priced bill was worth every penny. I couldn't help but compare how all the travel shows we watched when they would visit a true sushi chef in Japan who would just serve whatever fresh fish he had, was such a similar experience. The difference was, of course, not being in Japan and eating all local native fish and other creatures from their waters, but we still were able to try fish imported from places like Spain, Canada, Scotland, and our neighboring Santa Barbara. It was awesome sharing this special experience with the love of my life who was just as open minded trying everything the chef put in front of us!</Review>

<resp>None</resp><Pictures>None< /Pictures><Name>Monica Waggoner< /Name>< GmapID>

< user_name>
Tracy Thai< /user_name>
<time>1568089921506< /time><Response>None<//Response>< review>
The omakase experience at this restaurant is simply sub par for the price point.

The chef is very friendly when you start talking to him but he and his staff are very pretentious about his art, and undeservingly so. This sushi restaurant simply doesn't even come close to omakase from master sushi chefs in Seattle or Boston yet he is charging prices which significantly surpass any omakase with a master sushi chef in those other cities.

What's wrong here?
1st: Temperature. I had a mix of refrigerator cold albacore sushi with sauce, to nearly frozen crab and shrimp in a citrus based sauce, to warm, almost hot, rice in a nigiri with room temperature (and very tasty) tuna.
2nd: Flavor balance. Aside from the flavor and texture issues that come from the improper temperature, not a single dish I had left me with a complex favor of different kinds of umami. All dishes were extremely basic, utilizing the sweet flavor from the fish, salt from soy sauce or sour from citrus and vinegar. Nothing truly came together for an amazing treat for your taste buds (except the tuna). On top of that, for my last sushi I received a very spicy tuna roll that completely burned out my pallet, ruining all of the delicate sweet flavors I had in other dishes. I felt like I was assaulted with spice all of a sudden because he wanted me to stop eating (which I already said I was on my last bite so why do that?) And for scale, my typical maximum amount for eating sushi is an 8 piece nigiri or 1 specialty maki
3rd: Price. A sushi chef who can't get temperature and flavor balance right has no business being this expensive and pretentious.

What's right here?
1st: Quality. The chef knows how to find, select, and prepare top quality seafood and I do think that is valuable
2nd: Service. While most of my interactions with the staff were rather terse, I understand they have a lot of rude folks who come by who don't understand omakase so I was okay with a little bit of uneasiness there. I received a hot towel immediately after sitting, all of my dishes were promptly cleared away and my drink was refilled immediately. Fantastic service

The thing that really makes me sad to write this review is that he is a very good sushi chef and overall the sushi was very good, definitely above average. I would have been happy with a charge of about 70-75% of what I was charged because that is the value of the experience I had. Unfortunately, I definitely can not return because I refuse to pay $145 (for just myself) again for a slightly above average omakase (average across multiple cities across the US, not just LA).<//review>

< review>
I have gone to Chopsticks Express so many times over the years that I'm surprised I've never written a review. We probably get food here once a month if not more often. And, even though the ownership changed over the last year or two, it still has the same good taste and decent quality that you would hope for from a takeout restaurant.

I usually get the same dishes from any Chinese restaurant that I go to: kung pao chicken, sesame chicken, green bean chicken, and mixed vegetables with chicken. They're pretty darn tasty here and I've shown them in my images.

Now an FYI: it's not going to be the same type of quality food that you would get if spending $15 or $20 per plate at a fine dining restaurant, but for the price and for being take out, it's excellent.

Not only that, but the wait time is not that long, you can call in ahead of time, and the service is friendly and always professional.

One thing that I also like about this restaurant, is that you can order HAMBURGERS! They're even better than or at least on par with Habit Burger, and In-N-Out.

I'll definitely be coming back. I have been for years!</review>

<pics>None<//pics><text>This place is strictly for take out. Real small unassuming. You'd pass it up not even thinking about it. I went there on a whim. <Time>1505788477076</Time><response>None<//response>< review>
Call your order in advance so you won't have to wait in the tiny waiting area.  When I get an itch for hearty Chinese food, I call these guys in advance, drive over and get my drink at the nearby Grocery Outlet.  By the time I get my drink, my lunch order is ready.  All my single lunch orders are ready in 10 - 15 min.  I like their curry beef over rice; it's not on the menu, but they had no problem making it for me.  They also make cheeseburgers and fries, which was surprising to see in a Chinese take out joint.  They're ok burgers, maybe a little overcooked, but they come through in a pinch.  My recommendations from them: broccoli & beef over rice, basil chicken, and soy sauce chow mein with shrimp. Good portions too!< /review>

< text>
Urgent care centers are freestanding, walk-in medical facilities that provide care on a no-appointment basis and are often open for extended hours, including nights and weekends. Sometimes referred to a ‚Äúdoc in a box,‚Äù urgent care centers are a cost-effective alternative to emergency rooms for the treatment of  non-life-threatening medical situations such as cuts, sprains, simple bone fractures, flus and fevers, insect bites, infections, etc. Some centers provide basic laboratory and X-ray services, and most can run diagnostic tests and dispense prescriptions.

These care centers have existed in the United States for more than 30 years, and today there are approximately 8,800 facilities nationwide. They accommodate an average of 342 patients a week.

Centers can be owned by doctors, hospitals or corporations and take in approximately $13 billion in revenue annually. Many urgent care centers are staffed by nurse practitioners and physician assistants, in addition to at least one board-certified physician.< /text>

<rate>3</rate><text>Bay City Supermarket, it was nice to know ya!

Fresh Catch is, for all intents & purposes, Bay City with a new name.  Same layout, same products, same meat & seafood department.  Oh, wait!  There is one difference!  No saltwater aquarium as you enter.

Before visiting Caf√© 86 next door, I scoped out Fresh Catch to see what they had to offer.  Upon entering, a Thai dessert snack vendor sells various freshly prepared treats.  Desserts like kanom puang & kanom bang-jee.  Next to that, Thai trinkets & decorations are for sale with pricing varying from cheap to expensive.

Located on the right of the market, Azon's has turo-turo (food in warming trays) Filipino food available to purchase as a combo meal.  Azon's used to be located in the suite which will soon house the Neptune's restaurant, on the left of Canaan restaurant, in the same plaza.  A large dining area with a stage can accommodate a large amount of people  I'm assuming people having private events can make reservations here, but seriously, why would anyone want a birthday party in a supermarket?

The middle aisles have various packaged goods, from chips to fish sauce.  The rear of the market has the refrigerators/freezers for food, such as egg rolls & dumplings.  The meat & seafood section carries live fish/seafood, has free fish frying/steaming & seems fresh for the most part.

On the left of the building, more d√©cor & various knickknacks are for sale.  I believe there is watch repair offered, but I'm not for certain.

Parking is in a private lot.  Fresh Catch is the anchor store, located on the right of Luisa & Son's.

Fresh Catch seems to be respectable supermarket.  I have my local favs, like Island Pacific & 99 Ranch, but if I'm visiting Luisa & Son's and/or Caf√© 86, then I'll pop my head in to see what the weekly deals are.< /text><pics>None</pics><Resp>None< /Resp><gmap_id>0x80dd2da10b6249e5:0xb01c80b4f85feffc</gmap_id></record>

<UserId.>118119001893192250622<//UserId.><name>Sidney Kuo</name><time>1523399568160</time><rate>5</rate>< Review>
I love Firehouse Subs, and I've been eating them since I was on the east coast.  To me, the serve the perfect sandwich.  The bread is toasted to a nice crisp, the meats are flavorful and juicy, and the flavors are well-balanced, not too salty or sweet.

Among my favorite sandwiches include the Hook and Ladder--the honey ham is simply delicious and adds a savory sweetness to the sandwich that makes it very well balanced, the New York Steamer--probably the best corned beef and pastrami I've had outside of NYC, the Meatball sub, and the brisket sandwich, which has a nice smoky flavor to the brisket slices.  (My friend and I used to often joke it's smokier than most other BBQ joints in San Diego!)  In addition to the sandwiches, the cookies are great.

For any regional or national franchise, Firehouse Subs is definitely my go-to for sandwiches.<//Review>
